El Problem a Escolar, Resuelto 

De acuerdo con informaeiones publicadas por 
la prensa de Manila, la Legislatura filipina, respon- i 
diendo al clamor de la juventud escolar ante el 
problema de la instruction publica, creado anual- 
mente por el aumento del numero de ninos de 
edad escolar, ha votado una suma de setecientos mil 1 
pesos que Be distribuiran equitativanaente entre los 
municipios. Se cree que con esta suma habra lo su- 
ficiente para abrir el niime o necesario de esGuelas 
en todo el pais, y en lo que respecta particularmen. 
te a Negros Occidental, el deficit que monta 
en total a mds de P82,000. n 0 quedani cubier- 
^o con la cantidad destiaada a esta provincia, gra. 
cias a los esfuerzos desplegados tanto por la Junta 
provincial como por loa legisladores negren8es que 
a aquella prestaron su decidida cooperaeion. 

Nosotros, interesados como al qne m£s, por la 
Boluci6n del problema escolar en toda Filipioas en 
general y en esta provincia en particular, no po- 
demos menos de aplaudir el interns demostrado por 
la Legislatura que debido a las gestiones hechas 
por las Juntas provinciales y por los legisladores 
de cada provincia, y, mds aun, por la intervention 
del Gobernador general Murphy y el Presidente dei 
Senado Quezon, did prefertnte atenci6n al proble- 
ma en cuesti6n en sus primeras sesiones. Ha sido 
esto un rotundo mentis a las insinuacionos de que * 
nuestros prohomb'es en el Gobierno dan poca im- 
portancia a la instruccidn publica que, desde que se i| 
implants aqui la soberania americana, ha eonsti- 
tuido siem re un gran problema y una carga pesa- 
da para el erario publico, debido al creciente aumen- 
tp de escolares cada ano. Ahora les toca a los 
escolares el demostrar su amor al estudio, pro- 
curando sacar el mejor pa r tido posible de esta 
ayuda del Gobierno en lugar de dedicar parte de 
su tiempo a las diversiones que coma li cabarets 
y otros centros de distraction, les corrompen y dis- 
truyen su porvenir. j.

(By United Press) 
Washington, April 28— Within 
fdrfcy-eight hours after Arriving 
in Washington Somite President] 
Manu el Quezon suddenly decided 
turn to Manila immediately. 
This decision followed confer- 
ences with Secretary of War 
Dern, Senator Joseph T. Robin- 
son, Democratic lloor leader of 
the senate, Senator Tydintrs. 
chairman of the senate committee' 
on insular affairs, and President 
Roosevelt. 

Convinced that it is impossible 
to obtain any further action on the 
independence bill at this session 
of congress Mr. Quezon will sail 
for Europe on the He de Prance 
tojoinjiis family in Paris anxj. 
later come to the Philippines by- 
way of the Suez canal. 

It is understood that most of 
the mixed mission will leave with 
Mr. Quezon while the legislative 
mission will return by way 
of the Pacific. There is some 
talk of Speaker Roxas sailing 
with Senator Quezon. 

No agreement has been reach- 
ed between the supporters and 
opponents of the Hawes-Cutting- 
Hare bill but it is rumored that] 
a compromise may be reached 
accepting the measure with 
reservations. 

Mr. Quezon issued a statement 
to the press conceding that the! 
United States congress will not 
change or consider the Hawes | 
Cutting law until the Philippine 
legislature or a convention has! 
acted upon it. 

"I am therefore returning," 
he said, t4 to submit to the Phil-, 
ippine legislature my findings 
and recommend a future course." 
He emphasized the fact that he 
is still strongly opposed to the 
measure as it-stands.

Manila, April 28. 1938*1 why the result of the conference 

( between Senate President Que- 
zon with Prsident Rooseveft fs 
being concealed and why Quezon 
unexpectedly sojourned Europe 
and left the leadership to Senat- 
or Osmefia. 



Sir : 

The Filipino people has had su- 
preme faith of the undoubted sin- 
cerity of Senate President Que- 
zon's opposition to the Haw.es- 
Cutting Hare Law as an expres- 
sion of their stand on the ques- 
tion of independence. 

It is however futile to still be- 
lieve that the Senate President 
an^eu iYont. If he rea- 
lly had opposed, the Hawes-Cutting 
Law as the people believed him 
he might have done it during the 
time the measure is being consi- 
dered by the U. S. Congress, which 
according to the co-author of the 
measure, Mr. Hawes, all hi© ob- 
jection might have been attended 
to r^iake the law amiable to the 
Wishes of the Filipinos. 

The mixed mission headed by 
him with declarations to oppose 
the compromise independence law 
is still in Washington when 
the president, after three days 
announced his going to Euro- 
pe and left the leadership in the 
hands of Senator Osmena, chief of 
the seemingly hated mission. 

Threre is no reason to believe 



It is very clear ho that 
even when he is still in Europe 
his apparent opposition to the 
law is wanning. It is shown with 
his declarations and t\ciu which 
are inconsistent to hi^ alledge 
opposition to the law. 

The making is still going on 
and it is most probable that the ] 
mixed mission, now under the 
mandate of Osmena, shall bo made 
to bargain their vote for the 
approval of the law. Many times 
patriotism is defeated with person- 
al need? The Philippine- Legi la- 
ture being on the rear occupying 
a position seemingly on the " 
path" shall renounce their tr< 
cherous disguise and come out to 
the open as plain champions of the 
law. 

What a comedy! What a poli- 
tical footbal? 

Very respectfully 
JUAN M. MANANTAN^

Quezon And Family VfeiT 
Pope Fius XI At Vatican 



Zfffl 




Manila, May 11. -Dispatches re- 
ceived from Rome stated that 
Pope Pius XI today deceived Se- 
nate President Manuel L. Quezon 
and his family at the Vatican Pa- 
lace. The Philippine Senate Pres- 
ident was introduced to the Pope 
by the Rector of the American 
College. 

As was previously announ, ! 
in these columns, Senate Presi- 
dent Quezon plans to remain 
Europe after his visit to the Pope. 
In view of his illness he will stay 
in Switzerland with his family 
for about one year.

safe rcjectionists.

here that the senate president was 
In accord with Senator Osmena 
and Speaker Manuel Rox^3.

Man Returning Home 
From Meeting Killed 
By Train; Girl Dies 

/ _ ,.. i ^ % . 

Special .to. thu TRIBUNE 
Lucena, Tayubas, April 30. — A train carrying a delegation from 
.this province to welcome the Quezon mission iu Manila this morning, 
while passing through barrio Mayao last night, struck and killed Vic- 
tor Queano, 50, merchant, who was returning home from a meeting 
of "anti" candidates. 



Investigation revealed that the 
merchant, under the influence of 
liquor, was walking on the railroad 
tracks near the Lucena station. 
The locomotive was slowing down 
when it struck him. 

The merchant could not be iden- 
tified at once as he was badly man- 
gled. 



San Miguel, Bulacan, April 30.— 
Angelica Quison, 10, of barrio Pal- 



, talc, was instantly killed and Mar- 
cosa Ibaiiez, three, was wounded 
when a bolt of lightning struck at. 
group of people gathered around 
the sick bed of a relative at 3 
o'clock yesterday afternoon. 

The bolt set the house on fire, j 

(reducing it to ashes, but the sick 
people were removed to safety. Two I 
other girls with Marcoaa's parents j 

(emerged unhurt although th< y 

.were stunned by the lightning. 



MAGKAPILING SILA 



-\ f AGKAPILING sina Quezon at Osmefia, gayong sila'y nag- 
iYl kakasalungatan. Magkapiling at naaring magsama. Iyan 
av nasaksihan na, noon pa mang magtagpo sila sa Europa at no- 
ong naglalayag silang patungo sa Europa. 

At ngayong pauwi na siia rito ay lalo nang nagkakaunawa- 
an sila, sa gitna ng kanilang pagkakaibayo ng gawi. 

At makauwi lamang silang magkasama— upang makapagbi- 
:gay marahil ng magandang halimbawa— ay nag-antayan pa sila 
sa' Europa pagkaalis sa Amerika. Inantay ni Quezon sina Os- 
mefia, at ma^sasabay din sila ng pag-uwi rito, gayong maaari; 
silang magkahiwalay, mula sa Hongkong. 

Hindi nga, hindi pinahalagahan at hindi pahahalagahanj 
ang mapiling nais ng mga maibigin sa pagkakamkanyahang la-] 
ngoy Si Quezon— matangi na lamang kung hadlangan ng kan- 
yang sakit— ay makikisabay din kina Osmena At magkasama 
silang darating dito. At magkasamang bababa. 

Paano ngayon ang gagawin, sa harap ng ganyang pagsasa^ 
bay ng mga sasalubungin? . . 

Maaari pa kayang huwag magsama ang magsisisalubong? 

Mav palagay kaming sa harap ng magandang halimbawa 
ne mga sasalubungin, ang lahat ay dapat na magkaroon ng bait] 
at talino upang huwag patawa sa ibang nangagmamasid, sa oras: 
man lamang iyan ng pagsalubong. . .. nn , fl 

Ang pagsasama ay dapat na pagharian ng sigla at hinahon. 

Walang damdaming tanging dapat na makapaghan-sa 
oras na iyan— matangi sa galak at katuwaan. m , in .

INGLE RECEPTION 



But Pros Are Determined 
To Show Quezon That He 
Is No Longer Boss 

PROS GAIN^GROUNDS 



THIRTY HOUSE MEMBERS SAY 
THEY'LL DECIDE WHEN 
MISSIONS RETURN 



(Special to the Advertiser) 
MANILA, May 27.— The enemies 
of Hawes-Cutting act are exerting 
their efforts for only one official re- 
ception in honor of the two missions 
to avert any possible clash between 
the rival factions. 

The "pros" are determined to hold 
a separate reception in honor of Os- 
mena-Roxas party to show pres 
Quezon that he can't boss them any 
longer. The sweeping victory of the 
independeice followers in the prov- 
inces and in the city of Manila in 
their campion for acceptance is 
being viewed as a signal downfall of 
president Quezon and his thinning 
ranks. They now want to save the 
senate chief from further humilia- 
tions. 

, Thirty representatives have newly 
declared themselves open-minded in 
this national controversy. Their si- 
lence during the Quezon epoch was 
interpreted as rejection of the in- 
dependence bill. These same house 
members openly declared that they 
are waiting for the two missions be- 
fore giving their categorical view on | 
the Hawes-Cutting act.

HECTIC TIMES AHEAD 

WITH the repoi't that Senate President Quezon favors a na- 
tional convention to pass on the Hawes-Cutting act, it looks 
as if the Philippines were in for hectic times. 

If the act is accepted, then a convention, to draft the 
constitution, must meet not later than January 17 of next year. 
And before that convention can meet, another convention must 
decide whether to accept or reject the bill. That implies two 
elections between now and January 17. Doubtless many mem- 
bers of the legislature will want to be convention delegates. 
But the legislative session begins July 17 and continues till 
November 10. So what will happen the legislative session, 
with presumably most of the members out as candidates for 
the convention to accept or reject the act? In such case, the 
legislative session will have to be sacrificed, will be a farce. 

So we are left facing the prospect of a legislative session 
with little or no legislation, and the country's undergoing the 
throes of two elections, with the usual stirring times. As on 
the decision of the first convention will depend acceptance or 
rejection, and on that the fate of the Philippines, an even hotter 
election than usual may be expected. Elections in the Philip- 
pines are hot enough, but this one will be torrid.

Tayabas Indignant ,jj 
At Slap On QuezoJ 

Meeting Held, Resolution Passed 
Protesting Aquino's Attack 

Mammoth indignation meeting 
wiks held in Tayabas, Tayabaa, 
last night in protest to Senator 
Benigno Aquino's statements 
branding President Manuel Quezon 
as a tool of imperialists and call- 
ing the latter's stand as criminal, 
according to Ljon Malubay, act- 
ing provincial governor, who ar- 
rived in the city thia morning I i 
present the provincial board's 
resolution of protest to the de- 
partment of interior and labor. 

The provincial board, in a reso- 
lution unanimously adopted at the 
mass meeting. charged Aqumo 
with conduct unbecoming a i cw- 
aior aiid his attacks as unfounded I 
and insulting. Quezon is and will 
always be a favorite son of the 
province, the resolution stated, 
and insults against him will not 
pass without a general protest of 
indignation from the province. 

Governor Malubay, Board Mem- 
ber Pedro Insua and Municipal 
President Jose Reyes were the 
speakers. The president of the 
popular league in Tayabas also 
flayed Senator Aquino.

WHAT ABOUT IT? 

RECENTLY Mussolini, in an article on the State's dealing 
with crime, eulogized one of the popes who, in the case of 
a criminal apprehended 40 years after the commission of a 
murder, sternly ordered him put to death. 

It was only a few months ago that the Hon. Manuel Quezon, 
president of the senate, made a ten-strike with the public by 
declaring that the judge in the notorious Viala murder case 
would be investigated and by directing that such investigation 
be made, and, if he be found guilty of irregularities or official 
misconduct, that he be punished. 

In this case there was no need to wait 40 years. The judge 
is still there to be investigated, but— do you hear anything 
more of the investigation? 



9

que se practicase esta y dando toda clase de seguridades de que 
si dicho juez resultaba culpable de haber cometido irregulari- 
dades, o de haber observado una conducta impropia en el desem- 
peno de sus funciones oficiales, seria castigadp. 

En este caso, no era preciso esperar 40 anos. El juez esta 
ahi para ser sometido a expediente. Pero, £han oido ustedes 
decir algo mas acerca de la investigation?

Immediate return of Senate- 
Pres. Quezon to Washington to re- 
open negotiations for Philippine 
independence, after complete re-

Act by the Philippines, is suggest-

days after President Quezon had 
lett America for the Philippines. 

Th 2 Herald-Tribune, an authori- 
tative Kepublican organ, declares 
that nothing but flat rejection 
will enable Mr. Quezon to reopen 
the Philippine question and obtain 
a much better independence act. 
x'he daily points out that any 
compromise reached in the Philip- 
pines will defectively limit the 
success of new negotiations.

Quezon Urges Common Program 
For Future; Praises Good Faith , 
And Efforts of Legislative Mission 



Special to the TRIBUNE 
By CARLOS P. ROMULO 
Manajfing Kditor, TVT Publications 

Aboard the s. s. "Conte Rosso" at sea, June 3. — A common 
program for future action was urged today by Senate Pres- 
ident Quezon at a joint session of the two missions. The pre 
announced that although nothing definite has been concluded by 
himself, Senator Osmena and Speaker Roxas, the need to main- 
tain the national unity is manifest. Mr. Quezon freely acknowl- 
edged the fact that the legislative mission had exerted its best / 
efforts, and had worked in good faith. 

President Quezon called a meeting of the two missions late 
yesterday afternoon. Addressing the gathering, he said that ac- 
cording to the views expressed by the members of both bodfea, 
two fundamentals are well established: 
Mission Exerted Best Efforts, Acted 
In Good Faith, Senate Head Declares 

First: It is beyond all doubts that the legislative mission had 
exerted its best efforts to secure the best independence Jaw avail- 
able under the circumstances, and had acted in good faith; and 
Second: It is absolutely necessary to maintain national unity, 
, if it is desired* to" reach the goal of both the proponents~and op^ ] 
nonents of the bill, which is independence. 

President Quezon then went on: "This means that proponents 
of the bill as well as its opponents, should seek a common pro- 
gram for^utnre action. And I believe tha| there will be no dif- 
ficulty in that when the legislature is in possession of the essential 
L facts/" 

Quezon's Trip to Washington Was 
Beneficial, Fruitful, Osmena Says 

Senator Osmena, speaking in the name of the legislative mis- i 
sion, thanked President Quezon for aclmoWledgii bat the 

legislative mission had acted in good faith, He added: Che trip ► ol 
pKent Quezon to the United States was beneficial and fruitful 
o? sood results for the country. My Companions and f understand 
the sacrifice for. Quezon and the other members ol the mixed 
m j n underwent in going to Washington 

T i l(! members of both missions are optimistic. According to 
them the statements of President Quezon and Senator Osmena 
are indicative of the cordial relations between Ihem, and will P 
the way to mutual harmony and understanding.

the Legislature will stand be- 
hind the new chief executive. 
President Quezon's statement

"The message of Governor 
General Murphy has confirm- 
ed the impression he made 
on all of us who met him in 
Washington. It shows the 
excellent selection that Pre- 
sident Roosevelt has made of 
our chief executive, which 
also proves the great interest 
of the President in the wel- 
fare of our people. 

"Liberty, order and justice

social justice— is the keynote 
of t h?, JBeafiasE- iVoiection.ot.j 
human and property rights is

the present administration. I

planning in the administra-

with the Governor General.

will stand behind him."

Mission Leaves 
Washington For 
Manila Today 



(By Associated Press) 
WASHINGTON, April !».- -With 
plans for a quick onactmeni of the 
constitution of the future Philip^ 
pine republic, members of the Phil- 
ippine mission will leave Washing- 
ton tomorrow for Vancouver where 
they will board the Empress of Ca- 
nada, for Manila, expecting fco af- 
tend the legislative session. 

Manuel Quezon, head ol* the mis- 
sion, is expected here from New 
York tonight and will sail with the 
oi her members of the mi Lou 
aboard^ the Bmpros? of Canada 
which is due in Manila on April 
29. 

; Filipinos .here arc hopeful that, 
after a quick acceptance of the in 
dependence law by the in ui u 
legislature, action by the constitu- 
tional convention and President 
lioosevelt's approval of the con ti 
tution, the transition period can bo 
cut down to five or six yearf, bring- 
ing independence to the Philippines 
around 1940. 

Congressional leaders are insist eiri 
that there has been no promise & 
reduce the transition period.

Aba, diatuigo, pari Domingo! Kung batas HCH, 
alam ng mga 'anti' na ayaw ang bayan; kung batas M-T, 
alam nga nilang ibig ng bayan. 

Liiinawin sana ni Katoto, at htiwag siyang lagi nang i 

naghahangad makapangisda sa kalabuan. 

# # # * 

Kinikilala raw ng mga 'anti' ang katotoltanang "ang 
pag-ibig ng bayan sa batas ng kasarinlaai ay maliirap na 
mapaglaruan". 

Distingo rin! Kung batas ng totoong kasarinlan, oo 
nga, di-maaaring paglaruan ang bayan sa kanyang pag- 
kaibig; nguni, kung "oatas na bini-biro lamang, ang ba- 
ya'y siya na ring una-unang naglalaro, at da na kaila- 
ngang paglaruan pa ng iba. 

Kaya ba nang iginigiit nina Osrox ang kanilang ba- 
tg.s HCH, ang bayan ay nagkakangngingiwi sa pagtawa. 
Ang tawa niya'y may-kahalong habag sa "kainusentihan" 
o "kapilyuhan"" nila. 

Nguni't nang malamang ang misyon-Quczon ay nag- 
tamo ng iBang bagong batas, ng batas M-T.,^hmdi pa man 
nakararating dito ang buong "texto", ay kinasasabikan 
na't ipinagdiriwang ng bayan, 

Paano'y may labis na pagtitiwala ito kma Quezon* 
Masabi lamang gawa o pinagpaguran ni Quezon, ang ba- 

ja'y lipua na lipos na ng galak at pagtitiwala. 

• • * » 

Wala ngang sukat ipangai-wahe ang lalamunan ng' 
kaibigang "Taliba" — sakaling siya'y may-lalamunan,— 
sapagka't ang mga 'pro' ay hindi inaagawan ng mga 
'anti J ; mahanga'y ang mga ito ang inaagawan ng mga 
iyon. 

Kinikilala ng mga 'anti* na ang batas HCH ay kina 
Osrox; dapwa't ang di na maaaring aminin, ay maging 
kina Osrox pa rin ang batas Tydings-McDuffie. 

Hindi rin naman itinatanggr ng mga 'anti* na ang ba- 
tas HCH ay siyang pinasukan ng ilang pagbabago ng ba- 
tas T-M. Nguni't kailangan sana namang kilalanin ng 
mga 'pro' na ang "ilang kabaguhang" ito ay katumbas na 
halos ng buong batas na binago. Sapagka't kung hindi 
sa ganitong kabaguhan, yaong kasarinlang sinasabi sa 
batas HCH ay para lamang ng kasabihang kastilang "tie- 
ne pero no hay"— mayroong-wala. 

At ang misyon-Quezon ay siyang pmagkakaiuangan 
ng pagkaalis nitong salitang "wala", upang matira na la- 



mang ang "may-roon" 



Pag napalabo pa naman ng kasamang "Taliba" ang 
ganyang pagkalinaw-linaw na katotohanan, ay tala- 
gang . . . talaga!

COMPLETE INDEPENDENCE IN 1937 



MANILA, April 14. — Senate President Manuel L. 
Quezon was widely acclaimed upon his arrival in Hono- 
lulu. He predicted that complete independence will be gi- 
ven the Filipinos in 1937 or at an even earlier date. He 
{radioed President Franklin D/ Roosevelt to veto the ex- 
bise bill.

X Quezon, sa atas ng magandang hangad na. . . ihanap ng lu- 
nas ang pagsasalungatan ngayon.

Quezon sa pag-iiwi rito — na ligtas sa mga gambalang bandog ng 
mga tuntunin ng aduana! — ay tila hindi angkop na gamitin.

sa upang sabihin ang totoo ay... taglay na nga ni Quezon ang 
batas at nakikipag-isa na kina Osmena, .Roxas at Osias, wika nga 
ni McDuffie?

si Veloso.. hindi na dahil sa ano man. kundi dahil na dahil na la- 
mang sa "tangka niya, sa malas, na agawan pa si Quezon ng ta- 
gumpa^* sa pagkakaisa".

TSSION RETURNING FROM 
WASHINGTON 



Having completed their work in Wash- 
ington to their satisfaction, if published 
statements are to be given full credence, 
the Quezon independence mission to the 
United States s~t sail on April 7th, via 
the Empress of Canada, on their return 
trip to he Philippines. 

ft frs. Manuel L. Quezon and their three 
children together with Mr. and Mrs. Ar- 
senio N. Luz, Mrs. Felipe Buencamino and 
Mrs. Victor Buencamino lr.ft Manila on 
April 11th for Yokohama where they will 
meet Senate President Quezon and accom- 
pany him to Manila. 

Senatorial Candidate 

Since his return loathe Philippines 
in 1915. Don Sixto had not taken ac- 
tive part in politics —not in the sense 
of running for any elective ofnce. 
In the coming elections, however, he 
was persuaded upon by the Liga Ba- 
twnguena, a political faction in Ba- 
: tangas, to be the "pro" candidate f or 
' senator in the fifth district against 
Senate President Quezon. 

What his chances are in the coming 
elections can not be foretold. But, 
should a bachelor's luck be with him 
in politics. Don Sixto will be the sec- 
ond bachelor-senator. We have seve- 
ral bachelor-representatives, and one 
bachelor-senator in the person of Sen- 
ator Clarin. and a bachelor governor 
general. In this regard, speaking of 
the bachelor chief executive of the 
Philippines, Don Sixto humorously 
remarked: "I am afraid our governor 
creneral will not be able to follow my 
example: that of staying a bachelor 
to the ripe young age of /0. 

When asked why ke chose to remain 
a bachelor, the Grand Old MWi- of 
Batangas replied : "It is not that I 
want to be an eternal bachelor But 
during mv younger days, we did not 
have time to attend to love at .airs. 
We were so busy discussing how we 
could liberate the Philippines, and. 
between persecution by the Spaniards 
and meeting ourselves in secret halls, 
there was no time left for us to spend 
with girls. The truth is. that I for- 
got entirely things about love affairs 
when I was still a young man. Now 
I am already too old to marry any- 
way. So why should I not go ahead 
and remain a bachelor?"

"The victory of President Quezon is the triumph of the entire Fili- 
pino vcoplc f and we reiterate our adherence to his leadership. I say 
this in the name of the entire province of Negros*' « 

This was the salient statement yesterday of Representative Emilio 
Yulo, who arrived yesterday on board the s. s. Bisayds with the first 
group of the Negros delegation that will participate in the welcome 
for President Quezon. 

Another group is scheduled to arrive here on Saturday. 

Commenting on Negros politics, the delegates stated the antis will 
make a clean sweep of the province.

^ EDITOB1AL COLUMN }- 



Immediate Freedom Better 

Thinking Filipinos are against immediate indepen-! 
aence. They prefer a longer transition period for economic 
readjustment of the country. 

But with the present impositions upon the Philippines, 
like the excise tax on coconut oil, the limitations on sugar 
and other export products, it ia only wise that we prefer to 
be granted immediate freedom. For in the event indepen- 
dence is given us, we can in turn levy duties on American 
goods entering the Islands. That is fairness. 

We rejoice in Senate President Quezon's latest assur- 
ance that the Philippines mlF^e ^cbmpfefely independent 
on April 5, 1935. Not only that we can impose duties on 
American manufactured products, like automobiles, milk, 
and many others, but also we can find new markets for our 
sugar, copra t abaca, etc. The trouble is that at present we 
are too dependent on the United States, and we are tied 
up in the sense that we cannot make trade negotiations 
with other countries. 

In view of the apparent unfairness on the part of the 
American Congress, we prefer an immediate grant of inde- 
pendence. 



Una Manifestacion 

Precedentes En 
El Pantalan Hoy 



Una multitud monstrua de 
cien mil personas, la mayor 
que se ha formado jamas pa- 
ra dar la bienvenida a algu- 
no, sin exceptuar al fenador 
Harry B. Hawes hacl algu- 
nos anos, acudira este dia al 
pantalan para rendir homena- 
je al caudillo filipino Manuel 
L. Quezon y tributarle una 
prueba de su agradecimiento 
por su heroica labor en los 
Estados Unidos que ha dado 
como fruto la consecucion de 
la ley independista Tydings- 
McDuffie. 

La manifestacion de hoy 
• sera nacional. En ella toman 
parte pro vistas de grandes 
icartelones, bandas de musi- 
ca, arcos triunfales, delega- 



ciones nutridas de todas las 
provincias de Filipinas, uni- 
das ahora para honrar al cau- 
dillo y desagraviarle por las 
ingratas calumnias de que f ue 
objeto por sus detractores. 

Del Paiitalan No. 7 a su de- 
sembarco del "Empress of • 
Canada" el caudillo se dirigi- | 
ra a la Luneta y de aqui a la j 
Legislatura. Por la tarde se 
abriran las sesiones durante 
las cuales se aceptara la ley v 
independista. 

El recibimiento de este dia 
repercutira por su brillantez 
por todo el pais a pesar de las 
trabas que al mismo estan 
tratShd') de oponer los detrac- 
tores del caudillo.

TION OF DELGADO 

At the meeting; the other rii^ht 
of the Antis at Plaza Washington 
wfrer^e the orators of the Real Youth 
Party delivered speeches many of 
1he intelligent citizens of Cebu were 
reported to have been convinced 
of the irresponsibility of the youth? 
ful speakers. 

It is recalled that Anti as well 
as Pro newspapers in the country 
have gone on record as advocating 
for the retention of the leaderships 
of both Senator Sergio Osmena and 
President Manuel Quezoji.. And yet 
the Anti speakers from Manila did 
their level best to denounce the 
leadership of Senator Osmena. For 
this reason, many chorushed "Boo!" 

Jose Delgado, the Anti candidate 
for provincial board member had 
the audacity to call a leader of the 
Party "small potato" when 
asked to give a chance to have 
side of the Pros heard. The leader 
concerned, Attorney Bernardo Te- 
ves, bided his time. In the follow- 
ing open letter which he addres 
to Atty. Delgado. Atty. Teves gives, 
the pub/ic something illuminating 
about the Anti candidate.

or.

Quezon Will Gather Power in Party 
Hands If Victorious in Election 



In the event that his faction wins. 
Senate President Quezon will es- 
tablish here a party system of gov- 
ernment, with complete reorganiza- 
tion in the executive and legislative 
branches, it was learned from him 
last night. J 

The senate president would fix re- 
sponsibility in handling government 
affairs, so that when the people 
lose confidence in the party con- 
trolling the government they may 
effect a change by means of the 
' <reneral elections. 

It is understood that should the 
-antis" lose this election their lead- 
ers will urge their men in the gov- 
ernment to quit their posts and 
give way to the new party in po 

Wei% * • Quezon interviewed 

. president Quezon, ,. oH p ra ted 
last night at his Y.ow^jeiiei^ea 



; that he was still interested in the 
plan of introducing the party sys- 
tem of government. There is nc 
fixed responsibility under the pres- 
ent system, so that no one coulci 
be blamed when administration ib 
poor, he said. 

The senate president was enthu- 
siastic last night as he figured the 
results of the general elections, 
and reiterated that the "antis" will 
score a sweeping victory He told 
the Tribune last night even if Judge 
Sumulong loss, he will have still a 
majority of six, in the senate, and 
if Lloret also loss, as the pros 
Claim, the "antis" will still have 
a majority of four. 

The outcome of the elect on for 
representatives, according to Mr. 
Quezon, will further strengthen, 
the position of the "afltiB" compar- 
ed with the present hnc-up.

QUEZON WILL NOT MIND 
WHAT PALMA HAS TO SAY 

Senaio President Quezon announ- 
ced yesterday that he would not 
answer any articles or statements 
attributed to Rafael Palma. which 
may tend to attack him personally 
or his leadership. 

"Now that Palma is defeated" 
said President Quezon, "all I will 
do is to ignore him when I 
tempts to attack my person again/^J

Contributions to the last cam- 
paigns were noticeably slow in the 
coming. Every candidate, it seemed, 
was in need of money. Almost daily,

flooded with S. 0. S. telegrams ap-

short of needed cash. The sugar 
group failed, explained a high 
anti official, to rally behind Presi- 
dent Quezon. The senate president, 
in a recent conference with candi- 
dates, told them to make the most 
out of the situation and help one 
another.

MANILA, Mayo 21 (2ADI0) 
— Detoido al mal estad 0 del 
tiempo y a una ligera indispo- 
sition, el Pffsitlmtir QllP7.nn no 
podra salir manana para las 
Islas Bisayas, como se propo- 
nia. Sin embargo, se tiene en- 
jtendido que tan pronto como 
■mejore de salu pronto como eft* 
ijore de salud, saldra para Cebu, 
^para cumplir Jk prpmesa que 
habia hecho a los Antis de dicha 
Frovincia de visiter siquiera la 
cabecera de la misma. 

El Presidente Quezon tenia 
la intention de salir para las 
Islas del Sur manana, visitan- 
do primero las provincias de 
Hollo y Capiz, y luego Negro? 
Occidental, Negros Oriental y 



Qebu. Su presencia en estas 
provincias ha sido solicitada por 
sus partidarios, no solamente 
para ayudar a lcs candidatos 
Antis, sino tambien para darle 
un testimonio de gratitud por 
sus trabajos realizados en Ame- 
rica por la Causa del Pais. 

Se cree que lo que necesita el 
Presidente del Senado son po- 
cos dias de descanso soiamente, 
pues ha estado muy ocupado 
recientemente por sus viajes de 
propaganda electoral en favor 
del Senador Sison y del Ex-Se- 
nador Sumulong. Despues de 
corto descanso, se asegura que 
podrd realizar su anunciado 
viaje a Bisayas.

A FLORAL TRIBUTE TO RIZAL 




-14 




, f , , ii i . i, (Photo by Sun Studio) 

Manila's observance of Bazars birthday was featured this week by laying 
special emphasis on Rizal's love for books, in connection with Book Week. 
In the course of the program at the Luneta a large floral offering, in thh 
form of the opened pages of a book, was placed on the Rizal monument. This 
picture shows the floral piece being set in place, with Mrs. Aurora A . < ; 
Quezon playing the leading part.

MANILA J urno 30 (RADIO,.-. El nombramiento del 
Senador xeoiiio Sisoiv por el segundo distrlto -senatorial 
como Secretary cietTnterior (cargo que e] ocupaba antes 
de las elecciones), se considera hoy seguro El Senador 
Manuel L. Quezon, Caudillo de las Mayorias y el Gob°r- 
nador General Murphy, han llegado a un acuerdo sobre 
este nombramiento. El Secretario Singson ha insistido en 
su deseo de separarse del Gabinete, para atender a sus 
vastcs intereses personales. El Secretary Alas, del Depar- 
tamento de Obras Publicas y Comunicaciones', es el pro- 
bable Secretario de Hacienda. El Gobernador Cuenco es 
un fuerte candidate para la Secretaria de Obras Publicas 
y Comunicaciones, aunque se ha registrado ultimamente 
cierta oposicion a su nombramiento. El Secretario de Jus- 
ticia, Hon. Quirico Abeto sera renombrado nero dimitira 
despues de algunos meses, para ocupar otro 'cargo impor- 
tante en el Gobierno, la naturaleza del cu'al no se ha reve- 
lado. Para el cargo de Secretario del nuevo Departamento 
del Trabajo luchan el Ex-Senador' Jose G. Generoso y el 
Ex-Senador Teodoro Sandiko.

The New Gr<kr 

By EUGENIO BASADA 
"Respect Our Courts/' "Dtom- 
ors." "Regrettable," "Keep Invio- 
late." etc., arc all empty mouthin. 
agajtagrt the stand the President 
made in defense of the constitu- 
tion, the people, and the right ad- 
ministration of justice. All in all 
their criticism is tinctured with a 
greater desire of merely raising a 
voice of opposition against what- 
ever the President says or docs. 

In a case involving basic human 
rights affording room for abusive 
discretion, interpretation should 
not be impeded by rigid adherence 
to technicalities to defeat the spi- 
rit and purpose of the law. Sub- 
stitution of human caprices and 
sentiments for the spirit that 
gives life and substance to our 
law is per se a miscarriage of! 
justice. The court .should not be 
permeated with fanatical devotion 
and servility to form to allow its 
sanctified hall to become the stage 
for the whimsical exercise of equi- 
ty and justice.

squarely before them for decision, 
fearlessly and justly, as worthy 
disciples of Sir Edward Coke. Lord 
Chief Justice of England, centuries 
ago."

"Like in the eases of the teach- 
ing ban. the probation law, wom- 
an suffrage, and ihe teachers' gra- 
tuities, where President Quezon 
was manifestly wrong, his recent j 
attack on the judiciary is another 
child of his impulsiveness. 

"The Presidents grandiloquent I 
raid against the judicial ' depart- j 
ment of the government is not! 
only unbecoming of one holding! 
his exalted position, but brutal to 
numerous public servants who have i

human being, but this does not

Dr. Quezon vs. Pres. 
Quezon 

By Atty. INOCENGIO ROBETE 

Agno, Pangasinan 
In March, 1936, when Manuel L. 
Quezon was conferred with the de- 
gree of Doctor of Laws, honoris 
causa, by his AJma Mater, the 
"^University of Santo Tomas, he de 
clared in his speech, among others, 
the following: 

"Without popular faith in the 
administration of justice no demo- 
cratic government can long en 
dure"... 

"The common man in our coun- 
try does not ordinarily distinguish 
between the courts and the judges 
who preside over them. To him 
a judicial decision is not the man- 
date of the law but the pronounce- 
ment of men who sit in judgment 
over their fellowmen". . . 

"Not infrequently, technicalities 
of law or procedure defeat the 
1 ends of justice, thereby impairing 
the faith of our people in the ef- 
ficacy of our courts as the ultim- 
ate guardian Of their cherished 
rights and liberties. Such defects, 
however, can be remedied by legis-

SENTIDD HUM A NO 

/^UANDO murid aquel buen cab&llero que en vida se 11a- 
V mo Don Manuel Iriarte durante una fiesta habida en 
el Palacio de .Malacanang;,_el gobierno, en recompensa a 
sus servicios, otorgo generosamente a la viuda una bue- 
na .ayuda material. Esto, si no recordamos ma], ocurrio 
en tiempo del Gobernador General Davis. 
Hay ahora este caso: 

Joaquin Onglao, un guardia del Colegio de ' Agricul- 
tura de Los Banos, murio en manos de unos ladrones hace 
ya aiios; por haber muerto en la Hnea del deber, mientrasj 
vigilaba con celo una propiedad piiblica, la Junta de Re- , ! 
gentes pidio que se concediera al padre de Onglao una com-- 
pensaci6n de Fl,224. La peticion no fue sostenida por la 
Auclitoria, ni por la opinion emitida por el Profesor Cinco, 
con buenas razones legales naturalmente. 

En el caso Cuevo, ciertos elementos conservadoretf 
sostuvieron que dentro de la mas estricta interpretation de 
la ley, el Juzgado no se equivoc<5» al denegar la peticion de 
la esposa del obrero que murio ahogado por obedecer un 
mandate. El Pre sidente Quezon tuvo que intervener sos- 
teniendo la mterpi^a^ huma " 
na, y el priucipio de la justicia social quedo ymdicado. 

Joaquin Onglao perdio su vida en el servicio cum- 
pliendo con su obligacion ; no murio de un modo

NERO fiddled while Rome 
burned. Because Quezon is 
vacationing while important 
national problems await solution, 
political circles hum with insinua- 
tions that Mr. Quezon is playing a 
Nero role. 

In Quezon's parting- message, he 
indicated absolute satisfaction over 
conditions here, and said that he 
was "leaving the affairs of the 
. state in good hands." He had won 
his fight on the independence law. 
He had Had, it is believed, his way 
in the appointment of members of 
the cabinet. He had started both 
the Constitutional Convention and 
the legislative machineries running. 
Furthermore, he had seen to it that 
his own men would keep these ma- 
chineries running. 

Before he left, he held day-to-day 
(many of them behind closed doors; 
conferences with legislative leaders 
and ranking members of his party 
in the Convention and in our law- 
making bodies. He outlined to them, 
it is now reported, the program of 
legislation regarding which appeal 
ras also been made to Osmena for 
the minority's support. And it is 
this program, which many majority 
members of the legislature are 
starting to oppose, that has given 
rise to the comment that alls not 

^Reports there are that the senate 
resident may return to the Islands 
fter touching Singapore. They 
v that there are many unreveale<J 
asons for the possible return, but 



among them may be mentioned the 
rush report sent to him from the 
legislature last week. 

Senator Recto's assuming the 
position of majority floor leader 
when Sen. Avelino still believes 
that the position is his, does not 
speak well of the supposed harmo- 
ny obtaining in the Quezon ranks.
